<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13936381113186076402"><div>One of the world's most acclaimed adventure writers returns to the world of ancient Egypt with the stunning sequel to the<em> New York Times</em> bestselling <em>River God</em>. In the wake of a sixty-year war over the reign of the kingdoms of Egypt, two young pharaohs have risen to claim power, but only one can succeed, deciding the fate of his empire forever...<br /><br />The mission of Prince Nefer,</div></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13936381113186076402"><div>One of the world's most acclaimed adventure writers returns to the world of ancient Egypt with the stunning sequel to the<em> New York Times</em> bestselling <em>River God</em>. In the wake of a sixty-year war over the reign of the kingdoms of Egypt, two young pharaohs have risen to claim power, but only one can succeed, deciding the fate of his empire forever...<br /><br />The mission of Prince Nefer, rightful heir to the throne, is to rebuild a magnificent kingdom in the stark and tumbled ruins of the embattled city of Gallala. The desire of Lord Naja is to destroy his rival and rule the land with unholy supremacy. But Nefer has on his side the warlock Taita, a matchless ally and legendary priest of notorious powers...<br /><br />To see their dream come true, Nefer and Taita must stay one step ahead of the depraved assassin, survive the tortuous shadow of her ever-pursuing armies, and outwit the shocking betrayals of is own flesh and blood. As Nefer's courage increases, and as Taita's magic grows more beguiling, so grows stronger the power of their tireless enemies....<br /><br />Now, with the threat of tyranny and blood thundering closer and closer toward the vulnerable gates of Gallala, the ultimate battle for Egypt will begin...<br />
</div></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13936381113186076402">...more</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7314459-allie-cross" class="user" title="Allie Cross">Allie Cross</a>

        rated it

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer266767612">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15690594284331670288">My God, this is hilariously bad writing. How do I loathe thee? Let me count the ways.<br /><br />Obi wan Taita is so ridiculously overpowered I never felt like the "Good Guys" could fail. Yes, he did do the "These are not the droids you're looking for" scene. He also managed to call up a sandstorm, fake someone's death, and communicate telepathically. Since he can also control people as well, I view the whole story as his fucking about with the world for a sense of amusement. It certainly explains away a lo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15690594284331670288">My God, this is hilariously bad writing. How do I loathe thee? Let me count the ways.<br /><br />Obi wan Taita is so ridiculously overpowered I never felt like the "Good Guys" could fail. Yes, he did do the "These are not the droids you're looking for" scene. He also managed to call up a sandstorm, fake someone's death, and communicate telepathically. Since he can also control people as well, I view the whole story as his fucking about with the world for a sense of amusement. It certainly explains away a lot to me. :D<br /><br />The sex scenes were so hilariously ludicrous I'm convinced that Mr Smith has never bedded a woman, esp a virgin. Seriously, I want to hear from any woman that had three orgasms the first time she had sex. Everyone seemed to fall in love with the first person they so much as noticed; shockingly, these matches were also pretty much arranged by the Deux Ex Taita. I really got tired of reading about everyone's round buttocks. Seriously, that might be one of Amazon's unique phrases for this book with how many times he mentions it. <br /><br />There are other issues also, like the ridiculous cartoony villains and the severe lack of editing, but I don't really feel like bothering.<br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_55187004">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55187004" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/931455-dorothy" class="left imgcol" title="Dorothy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1407125020p2/931455.jpg" alt="Dorothy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/55187004?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 09, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/931455-dorothy" class="user" title="Dorothy">Dorothy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/931455-dorothy?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer55187004">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3521746527006675543">This book is a cross between an ancient Egyptian bodice-ripper and "The Return of the Jedi," with a little Marquis de Sade thrown in for good measure. I had read the first two books in the series, "River God" and "The Seventh Scroll," and had found them interesting enough to carry on to the third, but as far as I am concerned Smith went completely off the track with this one.<br /><br />Taita, the eunuch slave, was an enormously talented MAN in the first book. He used his knowledge in the service of his bel</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3521746527006675543">This book is a cross between an ancient Egyptian bodice-ripper and "The Return of the Jedi," with a little Marquis de Sade thrown in for good measure. I had read the first two books in the series, "River God" and "The Seventh Scroll," and had found them interesting enough to carry on to the third, but as far as I am concerned Smith went completely off the track with this one.<br /><br />Taita, the eunuch slave, was an enormously talented MAN in the first book. He used his knowledge in the service of his beloved mistress Lostris and her lover and his friend, Tanus. He was enormously talented but still human. In this one though, he has become a Jedi knight of the highest order. He practices mind control over the enemies of the young pharoah he now serves, Nefer, the grandson of Lostris.<br /><br />Oh, and that is another thing: It appears that Taita is now immortal and ageless. He sprints around like a young man and his age is never revealed, although various characters speculate that he is at least two hundred.<br /><br />So we have Taita fulfilling the role of Obi Wan Kenobi, Nefer is alternately Luke Skywalker and Han Solo, and his lady love Mintaka is a spirited Princess Leia. Give me a break! It is just a mish-mash and, at 735 pages, a very long mish-mash at that. About halfway through, I began skipping long passages of rape and mayhem and torture. Just not my cup of tea, thank you.<br /><br />I love the history of ancient Egypt and I love historical fiction - especially mysteries - based on the true history of that remarkable civilization. But this series, as far as I can tell, is pure fantasy, designed perhaps to appeal to the wet dreams of 14 year old boys. I'm not a boy and I'm certainly not 14 years old, so it's not for me. I won't be returning here. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3521746527006675543">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_102853617">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102853617" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3283584-bex" class="left imgcol" title="(´*•.¸?Bex?¸.•*´)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1400147426p2/3283584.jpg" alt="(´*•.¸?Bex?¸.•*´)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/102853617?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 15, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3283584-bex" class="user" title="(´*•.¸?Bex?¸.•*´)">(´*•.¸?Bex?¸.•*´)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3283584-bex?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer102853617">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15857244524588316178">The third in a series of books about ancient Egypt, WARLOCK returns to Taita, an eunuch slave who has served several pharaohs. Readers who met Taita in the first books of this series will love being able to read about him again in his latest mission. After getting a vision from the deceased Lostris, the queen Taita faithfully served and loved, he returns from his solitary life in the desert to help her grandson, Nefer Seti. Taita protects Nefer as he is thrust into a dangerous position at the yo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15857244524588316178">The third in a series of books about ancient Egypt, WARLOCK returns to Taita, an eunuch slave who has served several pharaohs. Readers who met Taita in the first books of this series will love being able to read about him again in his latest mission. After getting a vision from the deceased Lostris, the queen Taita faithfully served and loved, he returns from his solitary life in the desert to help her grandson, Nefer Seti. Taita protects Nefer as he is thrust into a dangerous position at the young age of fourteen. He aids Nefer in honing his natural warrior and intellectual abilities, all the while helping Nefer reclaim the throne from Naja, a traitor who killed pharaoh and assumed leadership of Egypt.<br />This book is exciting from the very beginning, opening with a scene of the Pharaohs fighting chariots racing towards battle. The plot keeps up its breakneck pace from there to the very end, filled with battles, tests of courage and endurance, as well as some magic and mystery. Wilbur Smith does a great job of adding extra twists to the story, which makes it all the more interesting. Smiths vivid language also draws the reader in, though in some scenes the action described is nauseatingly gruesome. Though this book is thick, the pages fly by in no time at all. Those who enjoyed RIVER GOD and SEVENTH SCROLL will love Warlock.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15857244524588316178">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/202967609?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 07, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5964540-charmaine-lloyd" class="user" title="Charmaine Lloyd">Charmaine Lloyd</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer202967609">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4794831972091929707">I love Wilbur Smith. He manages to write a book that espouses adventure, history, friendship and romance all at once. <br /><br />The central character Taita; though a eunuch, is a dashing “romantic” lead with his on-going love for Queen Lostris. In this world and time, it is refreshing to read of love beyond the physical. <br /><br />The story of ancient Egypt unfolds colourfully and the other lead characters are so relatable in their contrasts - Light and dark, love and hate, arrogance and compassion and the characte</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4794831972091929707">I love Wilbur Smith. He manages to write a book that espouses adventure, history, friendship and romance all at once. <br /><br />The central character Taita; though a eunuch, is a dashing “romantic” lead with his on-going love for Queen Lostris. In this world and time, it is refreshing to read of love beyond the physical. <br /><br />The story of ancient Egypt unfolds colourfully and the other lead characters are so relatable in their contrasts - Light and dark, love and hate, arrogance and compassion and the character development is relatable and realistic. <br /><br />The book is over a couple of hundred pages, but I got through it quickly as there is a plot behind every desert dune and it is very diffcult to put down. The only parts that I skimmed over were the Red Race and the last chariot fight – though intriguing, I found these too detailed and perhaps one chariot fight (detailed) too many. <br /><br />I have been reading Wilbur Smith since I was 13 years old. Whereas I have found that as an adult, I do not enjoy the style of writing of the other great story-telling authors that I read as a teenager, Wilbur Smith's style of writing is elegant and complements his story telling ability. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4794831972091929707">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_144369473">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144369473" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/595788-alex-telander" class="left imgcol" title="Alex Telander"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1326834904p2/595788.jpg" alt="Alex Telander" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/144369473?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 28, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/595788-alex-telander" class="user" title="Alex Telander">Alex Telander</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/595788-alex-telander?shelf=books-read-in-2001" class="actionLinkLite">books-read-in-2001</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer144369473">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12462475914686943996">There is a new magician to be added to the pantheon where the likes of Merlin and Gandalf reside: his name is Taita, a former eunuch slave, who is now the mighty and much-feared warlock of ancient Egypt.<br /><br />Wilbur Smith, bestselling author from South Africa, brings us his compelling sequel to River God, a novel of Egypt’s past, where a pharaoh and her eunuch slave evaded capture to fight against an evil conspiracy. The premise originally arose from a papyrus scroll that was brought to Smith, where t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12462475914686943996">There is a new magician to be added to the pantheon where the likes of Merlin and Gandalf reside: his name is Taita, a former eunuch slave, who is now the mighty and much-feared warlock of ancient Egypt.<br /><br />Wilbur Smith, bestselling author from South Africa, brings us his compelling sequel to River God, a novel of Egypt’s past, where a pharaoh and her eunuch slave evaded capture to fight against an evil conspiracy. The premise originally arose from a papyrus scroll that was brought to Smith, where these two characters were show to have existed at some time in the past. Smith then set about novelizing this account and creating the amazing world of River God. He does exactly the same in Warlock, with just as much gusto and skill.<br /><br />The lovely pharaoh Lostris is now long dead, but her slave, now a warlock – who must be over a hundred years in age – is still revered and feared by many. A new pharaoh, the young prince Nefer, is about to take the throne, his father having been recently assassinated and the killers remaining unknown. Since Nefer is too young to take the throne, Naja, the former pharaoh’s right hand man, automatically appoints himself regent of all Egypt. He hatches a devilish plan, unbeknownst to the prince, where he will unite with the enemy, the Hyksos who control northern Egypt, and get rid of Nefer, and together they will rule, abusing their power in as many ways as they can, meanwhile gaining untold riches.<br /><br />Wilbur Smith has a writing style that is entirely his own. His imagery reaches the point of over-description but never passes it, keeping the reader so entrenched in the world, that once they put the book down, they wonder if they are not actually in Egypt during the time of the pharaohs. Smith takes you through all the emotions, even if you don’t want to tag along for the ride, making you sad then happy by the turning of the page, appalled and shocked then satisfied and appeased.<br /><br />There is a lot in this book, where any reader can get entirely lost, whether it be in the love between prince Nefer and his Mintaka, or the anxious deception concocted by Naja, or the great battles fronted by Nefer and controlled by Taita. There is even some magic in there for all you fantasy buffs. This book, quite simply, has it all.<br /><br />Originally published on November 5th 2001.<br /><br />For over 500 book reviews, and over 40 exclusive author interviews (both audio and written), visit <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.bookbanter.net">BookBanter</a>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12462475914686943996">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span id="like_container_review_144369473" class="likeItContainer"><a href="/rating/voters/144369473?resource_type=Review" rel="nofollow" id="like_count_review_144369473"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a> · <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F37619.Warlock" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" rel="nofollow">Like</a></span> · <a href="/review/show/144369473?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1">see review</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_7252071">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7252071" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/445433-art-tirrell" class="left imgcol" title="Art Tirrell"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442452997p2/445433.jpg" alt="Art Tirrell" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/7252071?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 04, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/445433-art-tirrell" class="user" title="Art Tirrell">Art Tirrell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">readers who love adventure and romance</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/445433-art-tirrell?shelf=alltimefavorites" class="actionLinkLite">alltimefavorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7252071">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer968754786912096550">THE WONDERFUL TAITA HAS LOST HIS CHARM <br /><br />I've read Wilbur Smith's novels, "River God" and "The Seventh Scroll", and although I thought both went on too long and tried to do too much, I loved them for their originality and the excellent drawing of the principal character and narrator, the eunuch Taita. <br /><br />In Warlock, as in the two "Taita" novels mentioned above, Smith again tries to bite off a smidge too much scope but where the earlier stories were so strong I found myself able to overlook this flaw,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText968754786912096550">THE WONDERFUL TAITA HAS LOST HIS CHARM <br /><br />I've read Wilbur Smith's novels, "River God" and "The Seventh Scroll", and although I thought both went on too long and tried to do too much, I loved them for their originality and the excellent drawing of the principal character and narrator, the eunuch Taita. <br /><br />In Warlock, as in the two "Taita" novels mentioned above, Smith again tries to bite off a smidge too much scope but where the earlier stories were so strong I found myself able to overlook this flaw, now the novelty of the setting has worn off and this time the plot is less satisfying - much like Hollywood sequels that fail to measure up to the original films because they slavishly try to mimic the elements that made the original a success. <br /><br />Additionally (regrettably), Warlock grants POV's (points of view) to a veritable slew of characters, and the resulting stew ends up as a jumble of mid-paragraph POV swaps, pat dialogue, and thin characters. There's Taita, of course, but I much preferred him as the egotistical, lustful-but-incapable, boasting genius of River God and Seventh Scroll. There, his flaws glared but you'd roll your eyes and keep on loving him. Here, he is boringly perfect no matter who or what the opposition. <br /><br />Of the others, Young pharaoh Nefer is perhaps the most rounded. He experiences setbacks and tries harder the next time. Although we never really know him well enough to make the transfer into his skin, his character arc rings true as he grows toward manhood. Less convincing are the shallowly drawn love interests and the two bad guys. Between the antagonists they don't do a single redeeming thing in the entire story. Sorry, but I've come to like characters with a little depth, and here there isn't much to enjoy. <br /><br />To his credit, what Smith does give is a strongly imagined story painted in broad, colorful strokes. Smith is expert at setting the scene and Warlock holds the reader while trying hard to exploit the presumed familiarity of the reader with Taita. Sorry, it just doesn't convince. The plot is convoluted enough, but each "homestretch" is easily predictable, and I guess the broad strokes are to be expected when the writer is cranking out 650 page novels on a pace of one per year. <br /><br />In my experience with his works, Wilbur Smith is best when he uses his rich imagination to tackle an entirely new theme with fresh characters and an exciting original hook. The Courtney's come to mind. The initial novel was by far the best of the lot. Of course, as an author myself, I know starting fresh is also the most difficult way to write, and not the kind of thing that lends itself to the one-a-year pace this author has been keeping of late. <br /><br />In the end, I'm still a fan. I'll be reading the next one, and the one after that. <br /><br />If Wilbur Smith lived on the great lakes, he'd have written "The Secret Ever Keeps". He lives in Africa, so I had to do it for him. If you like Wilbur Smith, you'll love "The Secret Ever Keeps". Here's the Amazon page. <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1601640048/ref=cm_arms_pdp_dp/104-6302050-9055104" target="_blank">http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1601...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="968754786912096550">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a href="/review/show/169728748?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 23, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1781448-riobhcah" class="user" title="Riobhcah">Riobhcah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2959184-warlock" title="Paperback 9780312945992" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1781448-riobhcah?shelf=ancient-egypt-novels" class="actionLinkLite">ancient-egypt-novels</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1781448-riobhcah?shelf=egypt" class="actionLinkLite">egypt</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer169728748">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12271191407551723515">What a wonderful mystical adventure set in Ancient Egypt. This is one series of which I will be sad to reach the end. The wonderful Taita makes this book. Without him, it probably would not be as interesting. He has grown as a person until becoming one who lives in the spiritual dimension as well as the physical, as humans were meant to do according to Ancient Egyptian philosophy. So sad that many of us have lost this in so-called "modern" times. But there is some hope that it is being "discover</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12271191407551723515">What a wonderful mystical adventure set in Ancient Egypt. This is one series of which I will be sad to reach the end. The wonderful Taita makes this book. Without him, it probably would not be as interesting. He has grown as a person until becoming one who lives in the spiritual dimension as well as the physical, as humans were meant to do according to Ancient Egyptian philosophy. So sad that many of us have lost this in so-called "modern" times. But there is some hope that it is being "discovered" again. <br /><br />It's hard to believe that so many gave this book such a scathing review. I think the problem may be that there is an element of mysticism. Our so-called "modern" society is so skeptical when it comes to spirituality and mysticism -- some are even hostile to it. In Ancient Egypt, a society that in many ways was very superior to our own, a mystical meaning was seen in every facet of daily life. Humans are spiritual creatures and it's a shame that so many today would like to deny that. It's one of the reasons that our world is collapsing in on our heads. If we could get rid of the myth that ancient people's were superstitious and somehow inferior to "modern" society, and recover that realization that there is a mystical element in all things, we all would be a lot better off. This book maybe will at least make some realize that. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12271191407551723515">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer203616349">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15226809310430702984">I almost didn't read this book. I loved River God, but this one got disappointing reviews from others who loved River God. I will say that while I don't think it was nearly as good as River God, it's still a very good story, and well worth the time reading it.<br /><br />I liked the first person voice of Taita better in River God, but using this narrative form allowed the author to more easily be telling several different lines of narration at the same time, which was perfect for this story.<br /><br />It got a bit slo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15226809310430702984">I almost didn't read this book. I loved River God, but this one got disappointing reviews from others who loved River God. I will say that while I don't think it was nearly as good as River God, it's still a very good story, and well worth the time reading it.<br /><br />I liked the first person voice of Taita better in River God, but using this narrative form allowed the author to more easily be telling several different lines of narration at the same time, which was perfect for this story.<br /><br />It got a bit slow for a bit in the second half of the book, when the detail surrounding the preparation and running of the "Red Road" was being described, but with this exception, the story kept me engaged throughout. Lots of adventure, a little magic, and great storytelling.<br /><br />I'm going to stop at this one though, as the next in the series gets such universally terrible reviews. I think I will pick up and try some of Wilbur Smith's other books though, as I think he's truly a master of storytelling.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_428073789">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/428073789" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/13400725-will-hogarth" class="left imgcol" title="Will Hogarth"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442970595p2/13400725.jpg" alt="Will Hogarth" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/428073789?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 05, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/13400725-will-hogarth" class="user" title="Will Hogarth">Will Hogarth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer428073789">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13252649485413384467">There is no getting away with the fact that Wilbur Smith is a great wordsmith and story teller, but this book fell short of the mark for me.<br /><br />The characters are all well formed to a point where you cheer the heroes on and the plot is woven well to maintain pace, in what is a lengthy novel (over 500 pages) and at times the imagery conjured up by smith is second to none, but it still left me feeling underwhelmed. <br /><br />For me smith at times seemed to go too far with areas of gratuitous and sexual violence</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13252649485413384467">There is no getting away with the fact that Wilbur Smith is a great wordsmith and story teller, but this book fell short of the mark for me.<br /><br />The characters are all well formed to a point where you cheer the heroes on and the plot is woven well to maintain pace, in what is a lengthy novel (over 500 pages) and at times the imagery conjured up by smith is second to none, but it still left me feeling underwhelmed. <br /><br />For me smith at times seemed to go too far with areas of gratuitous and sexual violence, seaming to dwell too long over the detail of the event and thus distracting from the impact that the event would have had otherwise. Yes there are times when something needs to have more time spent over its telling and there are times when enough is enough and, in my opinion, Smith crossed that line to many times in Warlock<br /><br />I can see why this book has, generally, such a high rating, but for me – it misses the mark.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13252649485413384467">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10329885314824378039">Reread because I simply don't remember most of the story. I would strongly advise people to read this serial now in reverse order so that you can still enjoy this book without comparing this with the first or second book. <br />This book is like the second season of Spartacus, more blood, more gore, more sex and with another guy playing Spartacus. I tried to watch the second season, which has just more of everything except the heart of the show, the original actor. All the sex, gore and blood just couldn't make me respond enough to continue watching.<br /><br />So if you wanna enjoy this book, read the series in this sequence : Warlock, Seventh Scroll, River God.<br /><br />This way, you can enjoy all the books in increasing flavor without losing any joy.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1139564574">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1139564574" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5135898-lucas-rodriguez" class="left imgcol" title="Lucas Rodriguez"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1416281706p2/5135898.jpg" alt="Lucas Rodriguez" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1139564574?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 23, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5135898-lucas-rodriguez" class="user" title="Lucas Rodriguez">Lucas Rodriguez</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/125081.Hechicero" title="Paperback 9789875800830" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1139564574">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6163992707246426707">Hechicero' es la trepidante tercera entrega de la Saga de Egipto del autor, pero cronológicamente es la continuación oficial de la magnífica y soberbia 'Río Sagrado' (recuerden que el segundo tomo, 'El Séptimo papiro', ocurre en la actualidad y no el el Egipto Antigüo). Sin llegar a superar a la primera historia, es una increíble novela de aventuras y acción a las que tanto nos a acostumbrado este autor, y para todos aquellos que hayan quedado prendados de la majestuosidad del Egipto Antigüo nar</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6163992707246426707">Hechicero' es la trepidante tercera entrega de la Saga de Egipto del autor, pero cronológicamente es la continuación oficial de la magnífica y soberbia 'Río Sagrado' (recuerden que el segundo tomo, 'El Séptimo papiro', ocurre en la actualidad y no el el Egipto Antigüo). Sin llegar a superar a la primera historia, es una increíble novela de aventuras y acción a las que tanto nos a acostumbrado este autor, y para todos aquellos que hayan quedado prendados de la majestuosidad del Egipto Antigüo narrada previamente por Smith.<br /><br />La novela comienza describiendo son sumo detalle la traición hacia el Faraón Tamose por parte de su camarada y amigo de toda la vida Naja, quien lo asesina a traición para coronarse Faraón de Egipto. El príncipe Nefer es el próximo objetivo, ya que se interpone directamente en el camino del hicso hacia el trono. El viejo Mago entonces dedicará todos sus esfuerzos para proteger al joven para que, eventualmente, reclame su derecho al trono.<br /><br />Otra aventura épica se inicia de este modo, y vuelven por supuesto las exhaustivas descripciones que tanto maravillan, donde todo el lujo de detalle lo atrae a uno hacia la trama, llena de aventura, acción, romance, lujuria, una aventura épica con todas las letras.<br />A muchos les parecerá demasiado, ya que el autor no se guarda nada y tira toda la carne al asador: todas las escenas están descriptas, ya sean escenas de sexo, matanzas, asesinatos, absolutamente. Detalle que a muchos les encantará y otros lo leerán con suma morbosidad.<br /><br />Los personajes, aunque estereotipados, tienen carácter propio y se destacan muchísimo, ya sean buenos o tremendamente malvados: nadie tiene privilegios a la hora de estar de un lado u otro, no siempre el Bien sale ganando y viceversa. El Mago Taita sigue sorprendiendo con su poderosa sabiduría y su aún más inmenso poder, que parecería no tener límite. Lisa y llanamente es uno de sus mejores personajes, sino el mejor.<br /><br />No me gustaría continuar desmenuzando la trama, por eso les digo simplemente que vayan y consigan 'Río Sagrado' antes de leer esta entrega, ya que sino lo van a lamentar porque la historia de Taita no empieza aquí; también se puede tomar a la volada y leerlo, ya que no va a decepcionar, pero es recomendable lo anterior. Y si se quedan con ganas de más, la tercera y ¿última? aventura de Taita es 'El soberano del Nilo'.<br /><br />Lectura altamente recomendable, eso es seguro. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6163992707246426707">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15116259668645226769">As usual, Smith makes you feel as if you are right there along with the characters. I've read some reviews saying that he strays too much into the supernatural but he has done this before - the Umlimo in the Ballantyne books, for example. Ignore the sneerers; this is a great adventure story.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1209089239">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8256567157705262483">Terzo capitolo della serie "egizia" di Wilbur Smith incentrata sulla figura di Taita, lo schiavo "tuttofare" che, da schiavo eunuco, diventa persona libera e punto di riferimento per i vari faraoni che si sono succeduti nel corso della sua vita. In questa nuova avventura, quello che tutti ormai definiscono mago e stregone (ma, in realtà, Taita è solo un medico all'avanguardia ed un attento osservatore), deve affrontare la minaccia rappresentata da due falsi faraoni e contemporaneamente, districa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8256567157705262483">Terzo capitolo della serie "egizia" di Wilbur Smith incentrata sulla figura di Taita, lo schiavo "tuttofare" che, da schiavo eunuco, diventa persona libera e punto di riferimento per i vari faraoni che si sono succeduti nel corso della sua vita. In questa nuova avventura, quello che tutti ormai definiscono mago e stregone (ma, in realtà, Taita è solo un medico all'avanguardia ed un attento osservatore), deve affrontare la minaccia rappresentata da due falsi faraoni e contemporaneamente, districarsi tra varie peripezie, tradimenti, inganni, maghi e falsi dei ed istruire (non prima di avergli salvato la vita) il giovane faraone Nefer Seti, discendente della bellissima regina Lostris, già incontrata nel primo libro della saga. Romanzo davvero appassionante che, quindi, cattura il lettore e, nonostante le sue 600 e passa pagine, lo sprona ad andare avanti nella bellissima lettura. L'unico appunto che mi sento di dare al libro è che (sperando di non rovinarvi la lettura) le scene di sesso e stupro vengono descritte... con troppa dovizia di particolari!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8256567157705262483">...more</a>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1253571850">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2394296977982404157">I really enjoyed River God but I found the follow-up Warlock very disappointing. It is written in the 3rd person while River God was told in the first person by Taita who was a really likable and funny character. In Warlock Taita plays a much smaller role and is portrayed as an old and stern wizard/priest which totally didn't fit with his character from the previous book. Also this story introduces fantasy and magical elements which were nearly absent in River God.<br />All in all it's hard to even ca</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2394296977982404157">I really enjoyed River God but I found the follow-up Warlock very disappointing. It is written in the 3rd person while River God was told in the first person by Taita who was a really likable and funny character. In Warlock Taita plays a much smaller role and is portrayed as an old and stern wizard/priest which totally didn't fit with his character from the previous book. Also this story introduces fantasy and magical elements which were nearly absent in River God.<br />All in all it's hard to even call this a sequel to River God as it has very little in common with it in terms of style, theme and characters. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5866698770632334100">Took me 2 years to get through this book.<br />It was slow to start. Rather dull. Then when things finally got a bit exciting, it took a turn for the worse. Disturbing to read how one sister kills another by stabbing a knife into her private parts.<br />Sure, things like that may have happened at one time or another, by some sick individual, but it is uncomfortable to read it.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText5866698770632334100">Took me 2 years to get through this book.<br />It was slow to start. Rather dull. Then when things finally got a bit exciting, it took a turn for the worse. Disturbing to read how one sister kills another by stabbing a knife into her private parts.<br />Sure, things like that may have happened at one time or another, by some sick individual, but it is uncomfortable to read it. And seemingly perverse to write it.<br />Not a book I felt comfortable keeping, donating, or selling to anyone else. I destroyed my copy.<br />I won't be reading anything from this author ever again. Big turn off.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1288024376" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2596615-shawn" class="left imgcol" title="Shawn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1343445464p2/2596615.jpg" alt="Shawn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1288024376?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 09, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2596615-shawn" class="user" title="Shawn">Shawn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1288024376">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13627343969070027281">River God, a prequel to this book, was one of the best historical fiction books I have ever read and I had high hopes for Warlock. Admittedly, Taita was not one of my favorite characters in Smith's previous two books, River God/Seventh Scroll, mainly because he seems to be invincible and knows everything. One never gets the feeling he's ever in any significant danger. Nothing really changed about that in this book and he apparently also gained the ability to communicate with the Gods? That was t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13627343969070027281">River God, a prequel to this book, was one of the best historical fiction books I have ever read and I had high hopes for Warlock. Admittedly, Taita was not one of my favorite characters in Smith's previous two books, River God/Seventh Scroll, mainly because he seems to be invincible and knows everything. One never gets the feeling he's ever in any significant danger. Nothing really changed about that in this book and he apparently also gained the ability to communicate with the Gods? That was too much for me. Not to mention that it seems Mr. Smith decided there wasn't enough violence in River God/Seventh Scroll and decided to make up for it in Warlock. The amount and detail of physical and sexual violence in this book is appalling; especially towards the end, and much of it seems tacked on or exaggerated for effect. Don't get me wrong, I can handle violence in my reading, it's just that this was too gratuitous in my opinion. The result is that the violence distracts from the overall story rather than feeling like it's an organic part of the world Smith has created. The villains are written thinly and their dialogue is terrible as well. This is basically a very watered down version of River God that I wouldn't recommend to anyone who enjoyed that novel.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13627343969070027281">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4043.Wilbur_Smith">About Wilbur Smith</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/4043.Wilbur_Smith"><img alt="4043" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1337749545p2/4043.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer12185851528632439409">Wilbur Smith is the bestselling author of many novels, each meticulously researched on his numerous expeditions worldwide. His bestselling Courtney series includes <em>Assegai</em>, <em>The Sound of Thunder</em>, <em>Birds of Prey</em>, <em>Monsoon</em>, and <em>Blue Horizon</em>. His other books include <em>Those in Peril</em>, <em>River God</em>, <em>Warlock</em>, <em>The Seventh Scroll</em>, and <em>The Sunbird</em>. His books are now translated into twenty-six languages and have so</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12185851528632439409">Wilbur Smith is the bestselling author of many novels, each meticulously researched on his numerous expeditions worldwide. His bestselling Courtney series includes <em>Assegai</em>, <em>The Sound of Thunder</em>, <em>Birds of Prey</em>, <em>Monsoon</em>, and <em>Blue Horizon</em>. His other books include <em>Those in Peril</em>, <em>River God</em>, <em>Warlock</em>, <em>The Seventh Scroll</em>, and <em>The Sunbird</em>. His books are now translated into twenty-six languages and have sold over 120 million copies. Smith was born to a British family in Northern Rhodesia, now Zambia, in Central Africa, and attended Rhodes University in South Africa. He has homes in Cape Town, London, Switzerland and Malta.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/wilbursmith" target="_blank">http://us.macmillan.com/author/wilbur...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12185851528632439409">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/4043.Wilbur_Smith" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Wilbur Smith...</a>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_820396').observe('prototip:shown', function () {

              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
